### Michael Sikand (@michaelsikand)
_Fri Jul 10 16:26:44 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 283 · ↻ 22 · 💬 24 · [open on X](https://x.com/michaelsikand/status/2075617730242470376)

> Rosenblatt: Photonics short sellers have zero conviction and are preying on fear.
>
> They point out that short sellers have no real conviction in the short thesis and actually intend to buy the stocks back after covering before these companies smash earnings.
>
> Optical stocks have traded down for 1-2 months on two stories: fears that Chinese indium phosphide capacity crashes laser pricing for $LITE $COHR $AAOI, and reports that scale up CPO slips a year. 
>
> Rosenblatt figures Chinese players add 20-40% to their 2030 InP forecast, but they already model 2030 capacity running 40% behind demand. So even with new supply the industry is still short lasers. 
>
> They also argue the CPO "delay" is overblown. The process isn't delayed, only the ramp to volume. 2028 is now the inflection year and NPO fills the 2027 gap with nearly identical laser needs. Same photons, same suppliers, same thesis.
>
> You might see photonics red right now but the smart money is setting up to reload here ahead of earnings.
>
> $AAOI has been hit particularly hard and it's well known Rosenblatt has the highest street PT. So it's nice to see a bullish note here ahead of ER.
>
> "We expect AAOI to beat and raise and for 2Q26 to mark a watershed quarter where this starts happening consistently. We believe 2Q26 revenues can beat, and be above $200mn, with 800G sales to Amazon and Oracle as the primary driver of upside. The 3Q26 guidance should be ~$300mn with better GMs versus the ~30% level in 1H26"
>
> Can't wait to see photonics explode back soon.
>
> $LITE $COHR $AAOI $CIEN $VIAV $AXTI

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM4QTExbMAADZcV.jpg

### Melvin (@MelvinInvests)
_Fri Jul 10 16:40:26 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 437 · ↻ 79 · 💬 20 · [open on X](https://x.com/MelvinInvests/status/2075621178459513075)

> Goldman Sachs is projecting a 10x explosion in AI networking infrastructure from $15 billion in 2026 to $154 billion by 2028 (Save this). 
>
> As AI clusters scale from single racks to multi rack SuperPODs, the networking requirements change dramatically. 
>
> The current GB300 NVL72 architecture is a $15 billion TAM today and when you move to the Rubin Ultra NVL576 SuperPOD configuration and the TAM explodes to $154 billion, a 10x increase in a single architectural transition.  
>
> The key shift is that copper, which dominates scale-up networking inside today's racks, gives way to co-packaged optics at scale. 
>
> CPO alone is a $91 billion opportunity at scale but here is the thing though Copper does not disappear.
>
> In the NVL576 SuperPOD, copper backplane and flyover cables still account for $30.7 billion in TAM.  
>
> Copper remains irreplaceable for ultra-short distances inside the chassis, the physics simply haven't changed and that is the insight that makes Marvell so interesting right now.
>
> Marvell is the most underrated name in the entire AI infrastructure stack.
>
> The company is a dominant supplier of the copper switching, backplane and SerDes technology that lives inside every major AI rack today but that is only the beginning of the thesis. 
>
> Marvell also designs the custom AI ASICs, the XPUs that Google uses in TPUs, Amazon uses in Trainium, and Meta uses in its inference chips.  
>
> They are the arms dealer to all three of the largest hyperscalers in the world simultaneously and the numbers are starting to reflect what insiders already knew.
>
> Marvell posted record fiscal year 2026 revenue of $8.195 billion, up 42% year over year and they guided for FY27 revenue approaching $11 billion and FY28 approaching $15 billion.  
>
> Data center revenue now represents 76% of total sales, and the company has over 50 custom AI ASIC design wins entering production in FY2028-2029. 
>
> Marvell also owns Celestial AI's photonic fabric platform connects AI processors and memory using light instead of copper, meaning Marvell owns the copper layer today and is building the optical layer for tomorrow.  
>
> Most people look at Marvell and see a company that has already run but what they are missing is that the actual revenue from those 50+ design wins hasn't even started ramping yet.
>
> Extremely bullish on Marvell and make sure to follow me @MelvinInvests for more AI infrastructure ideas.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM4WI0qXAAAW9DP.jpg

### Devam Satasiya (@DSatasiya23)
_Fri Jul 10 17:18:30 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 5 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/DSatasiya23/status/2075630757679382963)

> Everyone thinks AI is limited by chips.
>
> It isn't.
>
> The biggest bottleneck today is moving data between them.
>
> An NVIDIA GPU can perform trillions of calculations every second.
>
> But much of that time is spent waiting for information to arrive from other chips. As AI clusters grow to tens of thousands of GPUs, the connections between them are becoming the real limitation, not the compute itself.
>
> Lightmatter looked at this problem and asked a different question.
>
> What if computers stopped moving data with electricity...
>
> ...and started moving it with light?
>
> Instead of electrons traveling through copper traces, Lightmatter uses silicon photonics to send information as photons.
>
> Light can carry more data, travel farther with lower energy loss, and multiple signals can share the same optical fiber at once.
>
> The crazy part is that they're not trying to build a faster GPU.
>
> They're trying to change how every GPU talks to every other GPU.
>
> It's like widening every highway in a city instead of making individual cars faster.
>
> That's why companies building frontier AI systems are paying attention.
>
> The next leap in AI performance might not come from a more powerful chip.
>
> It might come from changing the language chips use to communicate.
>
> Sometimes the biggest breakthrough isn't making the engine faster.
>
> It's replacing the roads.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM4fG_xa4AEvcgi.jpg

> The Trillion-Dollar Clean Energy Bottleneck: 5 Public Stocks Set to Fuel the Fusion Revolution
>
> The man who lit up the world with the blue LED is about to power it with infinite clean energy.
>
> Nobel Laureate Shuji Nakamura just officially unveiled his groundbreaking plan via Blue Laser Fusion to construct a massive 1-gigawatt laser fusion power plant by 2032.
>
> The Disruptive Fusion Moat Checklist:
>
> 🔹 Lasers Over Magnets: Diverging from legacy magnetic confinement systems, Nakamura is utilizing specialized high-pulse inertial lasers amplified 100,000x via optical cavities to achieve self-sustaining energy net-gain.
>
> 🔹 Zero Radioactive Waste: The platform targets a non-radioactive hydrogen-boron (HB11) fuel cycle—meaning zero harmful neutrons, zero meltdown risks, and absolutely zero long-lived toxic waste.
>
> 🔹 The Ultimate Data Center Solution: As AI hyperscalers exhaust local grids, on-site, baseline, zero-emission laser fusion will become the holy grail infrastructure asset of the next decade.
>
> While Blue Laser Fusion is currently a highly backed private venture (funded by SoftBank, Toyota's SPARX, and Itochu), the massive capital flows pouring into laser hardware, optics, and specialized power electronics are about to trigger a historic multi-billion dollar public supply chain supercycle.
>
> The commercial race for infinite power has officially hit a structural inflection point. Are you positioned for the energy hardware boom, or still chasing speculative applications?
>
> 5 Public Stocks Set to Benefit from the Laser Fusion Boom:
>
> 1. Coherent Corp. (COHR) ⚡What they do / Potential: Manufactures the ultra-high-power industrial laser systems, optics, and precision crystal substrates required to generate and guide hyper-amplified beam pulses into the fusion fuel core.
>
> 2. IPG Photonics Corporation (IPGP) 🔬What they do / Potential: A global pioneer in high-power fiber lasers, uniquely positioned to supply the underlying high-efficiency, multi-kilowatt rapid-firing continuous laser modules necessary to scale up commercial power plants.
>
> 3. L3Harris Technologies, Inc. (LHX) 🛡️What they do / Potential: Builds complex photonic control systems, advanced target tracking tracking arrays, and optical cavities engineered to perfectly time microsecond laser impacts against fusion fuel pellets.
>
> 4. Materion Corporation (MTRN) 🧱What they do / Potential: Supplies advanced high-purity beryllium, specialized alloys, and thermal management metals critical to lining the internal walls of containment chambers to absorb and stabilize intense fusion energy output.
>
> 5. Perma-Fix Environmental Services, Inc. (PESI) ☢️What they do / Potential: While modern laser fusion is exceptionally clean, their specialized nuclear engineering and reactor waste maintenance frameworks will hold primary service value as standard infrastructure protocols roll out.

### 💭 (@euklbe)
_Fri Jul 10 18:10:24 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/euklbe/status/2075643818947608973)

> Q: This seems like a quite complex field to understand.
>
> A: The principle is very similar to urban planning. Frequently used data is placed close by, and occasionally used data is placed further away. Since speed is crucial when data moves, it's the principle of building a customized data transportation network—just like choosing a motorcycle or an express bus depending on the environment. A prime example of a global company specializing in building these communication networks is Broadcom.
>
> Q: To the general public, tech companies might all look similar, but in reality, their unique roles and exclusive technological territories are firmly divided.
>
> A: That's right. The key is to transfer data among HBM, HBF, and GPU as quickly as possible to reduce latency. Currently, data is transmitted as electrical signals through copper wires, but there is a physical limitation where the signal speed drops due to the copper's resistance. To overcome this, the method of transmitting data using 'light' (optical communication) instead of electricity has emerged, which is why silicon photonics-related companies are gaining attention recently. A prime example is the 'InfiniBand' technology acquired by NVIDIA, which handles optical communication between modules. Like the Strait of Hormuz, these monopoly technology companies, holding tight to the bottlenecks in the global chip supply chain, are positioned in their respective fields.
>
> Q: When do you expect HBF to be commercialized?
>
> A: Research is likely progressing with a target of 2027, so I expect the first product to be released around 2028. It is highly likely that one of NVIDIA, AMD, or Google will introduce the first commercialized product. The primary reason Big Tech companies are interested in HBF is to reduce their dependence on Korean companies. If they solely use HBM, they can't escape Samsung Electronics and SK Hynix, but adopting HBF gives them alternatives to collaborate with American companies like SanDisk or Micron.
>
> However, I believe that attempt will ultimately not hold much significance. I argue that to extract the absolute best performance, HBM and HBF must be configured together.
>
> Q: If the environment requires both types of memory, doesn't that create an absolutely advantageous situation for Samsung Electronics and SK Hynix, since they can produce both HBM and HBF?
>
> A: Yes, it does. Because both companies already firmly possess world-class semiconductor stacking and packaging technologies through HBM production, they are naturally bound to hold the upper hand in the next-generation memory competition as well.

### Athu (@athuinvests)
_Fri Jul 10 18:10:36 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 181 · ↻ 16 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/athuinvests/status/2075643866481377290)

> Rosenblatt releases bullish report on $AAOI and other optical names before earnings season.
>
> The report cuts through the noise on why the optical sector has been weak the last few weeks. Two main fears stand out, both of which Rosenblatt sees as overstated. 
>
> This looks like a huge buying opportunity.
>
> 1) China InP capacity
>
> > The worry is that Chinese players are ramping hard and will flood the market with cheap lasers, hurting names like $LITE and $COHR.
>
> > Chinese capacity could add 20-40% on top of the 2030 baseline, but supply still falls well short of demand.
>
> > The Chinese are also still behind on the tech. Lower-end lasers are doing fine for 800G and below, but they don’t yet have enough production 200G EMLs for 1.6T+ transceivers or the high-power lasers needed for real CPO scale. 
>
> > Western order books are full through 2027 and into 2028, with $NVDA securing a lot of the supply and $AMD now looking to the same names.
>
> 2) CPO timing
>
> > The early smaller programs remain on track for 2H26 build and 2027 shipments. 
>
> > The bigger scale-up volume looks more likely to hit in 2028, with NPO picking up a lot of the slack in 2027. 
>
> > Other concerns like network flattening from larger switches were already modeled. Exploding XPU demand more than offsets any reduction in transceivers per switch. 
>
> > VCSELs could play a role in some intermediate NPO designs, but high-power InP stays central for flagship CPO performance.
>
> --------------------------------------------------------------
>
> Short sellers: 
>
> - One thing that stood out is what the short sellers are actually saying. Many have been using the China InP story to push the weakness, but most don’t appear to have strong conviction in it. 
> - Multiple shorts told Rosenblatt they plan to close positions ahead of late July and early August earnings and then buy back into optical names in 2027 for the CPO ramp in 2028-2030. 
>
> That’s not something you’d hear if they truly believed the oversupply thesis.
>
> --------------------------------------------------------------
>
> Overall, I feel this is bullish for optical names like $SIVE, $AAOI, $LITE, $COHR, $TSEM, $VIAV, etc. 
>
> It also aligns with what I mentioned before that July end to August start should be a great time for optics as the earnings season plays out and some of this noise clears.
>
> Long photonics!

### Black Hole (@konstructivizm)
_Fri Jul 10 18:22:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 78 · ↻ 13 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/konstructivizm/status/2075646736484245804)

> Physicists Just Extracted Energy from a “Black Hole” — Without Any Rotation
>
> In 1969, Roger Penrose proposed a mind-bending way to steal energy from a rotating black hole. Drop an object into the ergosphere (the zone just outside the event horizon), let it split, and one piece falls in while the other flies out with more energy than you started with. It sounded like science fiction.
>
> More than 50 years later, researchers at the City University of New York have made a version of this effect real — in a lab, without any actual black hole or physical spinning.
>
> The Breakthrough
> Instead of building a rotating object, the team created a ring-shaped network of resonators whose properties change over time in a carefully controlled way (spatiotemporal modulation). This synthetic “motion” mimics rotation through the Floquet effect, allowing them to observe superradiance — waves coming out with more energy than they went in.
>
> This is the first experimental confirmation of the Zel’dovich effect (an extension of Penrose’s idea) using purely electromagnetic waves in a non-rotating system.
>
> Why It Matters
> It bridges theoretical astrophysics with real-world photonics.
> The experiment opens doors to new types of ultra-efficient amplifiers and wave generators.
> It lets scientists study wave-matter interactions in rotating frames without needing massive, fast-spinning hardware.
>
> Previous experiments used spinning disks or cylinders, but this new approach eliminates mechanical rotation entirely — a cleaner, more elegant demonstration.
>
> While we’re still far from harvesting energy from real black holes, these tabletop analogs help us understand fundamental physics and could lead to revolutionary technologies in wave manipulation and energy harvesting.

### carlosfagar (@carlosfagar)
_Fri Jul 10 18:29:50 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/carlosfagar/status/2075648709300248993)

> $MRVL (Marvell Technology) es uno de los grandes beneficiarios silenciosos (y cada vez más ruidosos) del boom de la infraestructura de IA. Aquí te detallo los puntos clave que pediste de forma clara y actualizada (datos a julio 2026).
>
> 1. - La inversión de NVIDIA ($2.000 millones)
> El 31 de marzo de 2026, NVIDIA anunció una inversión de $2 mil millones en Marvell + una alianza estratégica profunda.
> Marvell se integra al ecosistema NVIDIA a través de NVLink Fusion, lo que permite que los custom XPUs (aceleradores de IA) y soluciones de networking de Marvell funcionen de forma nativa y compatible con la infraestructura de NVIDIA (incluyendo Vera CPU, ConnectX NICs, BlueField DPUs, NVLink y Spectrum-X switches).
> Además, colaborarán en silicon photonics y en llevar IA a redes de telecomunicaciones (AI-RAN para 5G/6G).
> ¿Por qué es tan importante?
> •  Valida a Marvell como proveedor de custom silicon de primer nivel.
> •  Da a los hyperscalers más flexibilidad: pueden usar GPUs NVIDIA + custom XPUs de Marvell en el mismo rack sin problemas de compatibilidad.
> •  Es una “co-opetición” inteligente: Marvell ayuda a escalar el ecosistema NVIDIA mientras compite en custom ASICs y óptica.
> El mercado reaccionó muy bien: MRVL subió fuerte ese día.

### carlosfagar (@carlosfagar)
_Fri Jul 10 18:30:02 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/carlosfagar/status/2075648758381990205)

> 2. Ventajas competitivas (el verdadero moat)
> Marvell tiene varias capas de ventaja:
> •  Liderazgo en óptica de alta velocidad: Es el referente mundial en PAM4 DSPs. Fue el primero en lanzar DSP de 1.6T en 5nm (Nova) y luego en 3nm (plataforma Ara). Sus productos Ara T, Ara X y Petra están ganando tracción masiva en 800G/1.6T para clusters de IA.
> •  Custom Silicon / XPUs de primer nivel: Junto con Broadcom, es de las únicas dos compañías capaces de diseñar y llevar a producción en volumen ASICs/XPUs extremadamente complejos (cientos de miles de millones de transistores). Trabaja con AWS (Trainium), Microsoft (Maia), Meta (MTIA) y Google. Ofrece un servicio end-to-end (arquitectura + IP + diseño + packaging avanzado + soporte de fabricación).
> •  Portfolio completo de data infrastructure: No solo hace una cosa. Tiene switches Ethernet de alto rendimiento (Teralynx hasta 51.2 Tbps), retimers PCIe 6 (Alaska P), CXL (Structera), Active Electrical Cables (AEC), Co-Packaged Optics (CPO) y silicon photonics. Es uno de los pocos que puede proveer casi todo el “nervio” de un data center de IA.
> •  IP y tecnología propietaria fuerte: Excelente portafolio de SerDes de ultra alta velocidad, analog/mixed-signal de bajo consumo y tecnologías de packaging avanzado (chiplets, CPO, HBM custom).
> •  Adquisición estratégica: Compró Celestial AI (óptica fotónica para scale-up interconnect), que potencia su posición en óptica de próxima generación.
> •  Altas barreras de entrada: Los design wins de custom silicon son multi-generacionales y crean switching costs muy altos. Una vez que un hyperscaler diseña su XPU con Marvell, es muy difícil y caro cambiar.

### carlosfagar (@carlosfagar)
_Fri Jul 10 18:30:03 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/carlosfagar/status/2075648763457085711)

> 3. ¿Qué productos hace realmente?
> Marvell se ha transformado en una compañía data infrastructure / AI-first. Sus productos principales hoy son:
> •  Custom AI accelerators (XPUs) y silicio adjunto (XPU-attach, NICs, CXL).
> •  Optical DSPs de alta velocidad (800G y 1.6T PAM4) → el motor de crecimiento actual.
> •  Switches Ethernet de data center (Teralynx family, hasta 51.2 Tbps, baja latencia).
> •  Interconnects de alta velocidad: Active Electrical Cables (AEC), PCIe retimers, CXL, silicon photonics y Co-Packaged Optics (CPO).
> •  Storage controllers (HDD y SSD) — sigue siendo un negocio sólido pero ya no es el principal driver.
> •  Otros (menor peso): DPUs, soluciones enterprise y carrier (5G).
> El Data Center ya representa ~75-76% de los ingresos y crece mucho más rápido que el resto.

### favoritbookshop🚢 (@favoritbookshop)
_Fri Jul 10 18:52:39 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/favoritbookshop/status/2075654452158300439)

> AI's Next Bottleneck: Networking & Optics Could Become the Biggest Winners of the AI Infrastructure Cycle
> The AI investment narrative has largely centered on GPUs and compute. However, the next phase of the AI supercycle may be determined by an entirely different segment: networking and optical infrastructure.
> As AI clusters expand from thousands to millions of accelerators, moving data efficiently becomes just as important as generating compute power. Faster GPUs create little value if they spend time waiting for information to arrive.
> That is why the Networking & Optics Landscape deserves close attention.
> Current industry data highlights an unprecedented supply-demand imbalance:
> Coherent's Indium Phosphide (InP) lasers are reportedly sold out through 2027, supported by an exceptional 4x book-to-bill ratio.
> Ciena reached a record $7B order backlog, reflecting sustained demand from hyperscalers and telecom infrastructure.
> Lumentum expects approximately 77% revenue growth for FY2026, one of the strongest growth outlooks across semiconductor-adjacent industries.
> Unlike many AI segments where additional manufacturing capacity is gradually coming online, optical networking remains a genuine bottleneck. Every new AI data center requires high-speed optical interconnects, silicon photonics, switches, and advanced networking hardware before GPUs can operate at scale.
> The companies highlighted in this landscape represent nearly every critical layer of the ecosystem:
> Switching & Systems: Cisco, Arista, Ciena
> Interconnect Silicon: Marvell, Astera Labs, Credo, Macom
> Lasers & Optical Components: Coherent, Lumentum, Corning, Applied Optoelectronics
> Manufacturing: Fabrinet
> China Optics: Innolight, Eoptolink
> Silicon Photonics (Private): Lightmatter, Ayar Labs
> Crypto Investors Should Pay Attention
> Blockchain investors often focus on tokens directly tied to AI narratives, but the real capital cycle frequently begins with physical infrastructure.
> As hyperscalers continue deploying massive AI clusters, companies supplying networking hardware and optical components may capture significant value before downstream AI applications fully mature.
> The lesson for crypto markets is familiar: infrastructure tends to outperform during the early stages of transformational technology cycles. The same pattern previously benefited semiconductor manufacturers, cloud providers, and blockchain infrastructure projects.
> The AI race is no longer just about faster chips—it's increasingly about moving data at unprecedented speed. Until supply catches demand, networking and optics remain one of the strongest structural themes across the entire AI ecosystem.
> #AI #Crypto #Stocks #Tech

### My name is M. Only M (@musicandsoularg)
_Fri Jul 10 21:10:57 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 14 · ↻ 2 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/musicandsoularg/status/2075689255666352593)

> AVANCES EN TELEPORTACIÓN CUÁNTICA: EL CAMINO HACIA UN INTERNET ULTRASEGURO
>
> Investigadores de la Universidad de Ciencia y Tecnología de China han logrado un avance significativo en la teleportación cuántica a gran escala utilizando redes de fibra óptica de larga distancia, un paso crucial para el desarrollo de un internet cuántico prácticamente incorruptible.
>
> El experimento aprovecha el entrelazamiento cuántico, el fenómeno que Albert Einstein denominó "acción fantasmal a la distancia", donde el estado de dos partículas vinculadas se correlaciona sin importar la separación física entre ellas. Este sistema permite transferir estados cuánticos (información de la partícula) entre nodos distantes sin necesidad de desplazar la materia física en sí.
>
> Sin embargo, es importante aclarar un mito común en la física: este proceso no permite la comunicación instantánea ni supera la velocidad de la luz. Para que la teleportación cuántica se complete con éxito, los científicos siempre necesitan enviar datos adicionales a través de canales tradicionales (como cables de fibra óptica convencionales), lo que limita la velocidad final de la transmisión a los límites impuestos por la teoría de la relatividad.
>
> El verdadero hito de este avance no radica en la velocidad, sino en la seguridad y la fidelidad de la red. Al entrelazar las partículas, cualquier intento de interceptar, medir o espiar la información destruye de inmediato el estado cuántico, creando un ecosistema criptográfico inmune a los ciberataques y garantizando una privacidad digital absoluta para el futuro.
>
> Fuente: University of Science and Technology of China | Nature Photonics | MIT Technology Review

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 10 21:27:22 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 212 · ↻ 45 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2075693388158894328)

> Mirae Asset Securities: AI Bottleneck Issue
>
> Power Bottleneck
>
> > The Moment for Analog Semiconductors: The value of the analog domain, where Moore's Law does not apply, is exploding, giving suppliers overwhelming pricing power. Major players like TI, NXP, and Infineon are proving this dominant supplier market by executing synchronized price hikes in 2026.
>
> > The Physics of 12,500 Amperes and 800V DC: In ultra-high-density AI racks of 600kW to 1MW, sticking to traditional 48V power distribution causes the current to skyrocket to 12,500A, making operations impossible due to heat loss. Therefore, shifting the architecture to 800V to reduce the current to 750A and cut copper requirements by 45% is a physical inevitability.
>
> > Vertical Power Delivery (VPD): To prevent loss and voltage fluctuations during the "last inch" of stepping down to the GPU core voltage (around 0.7V), VPD—essentially the "CPO of the power world"—is emerging, which places the power converter directly beneath the GPU die.
>
> Signal & Photonics Bottleneck
>
> > Distance-Based Redistribution of Copper and Optics: The simplistic narrative that "optics will completely wipe out copper" is incorrect. A distance-based redistribution is intensifying, where copper and analog handle short distances (the scale-up domain) and optics take over long distances (rack-to-rack connectivity).
>
> > Semtech’s Analog Magic: In 200G/lane high-speed communication, Semtech's technology is garnering massive attention by completely eliminating DSPs (Digital Signal Processors)—which consume heavy power and cause latency—and correcting signals using only Analog Equalizers. This reduces power consumption by tenfold and slashes latency from nanoseconds (ns) to picoseconds (ps).
>
> > The Real Bottleneck in Optical Tech is the 'Light Source': While Co-Packaged Optics (CPO) is the correct long-term direction, the realistic winners for the next 2 to 3 years are Near-Packaged Optics (NPO) and 1.6T pluggable modules. The true bottlenecks in optical communication lie below the finished optical module layer: InP (Indium Phosphide) substrates, Continuous Wave (CW) laser sources, Photonics-SOI wafers (monopolized by Soitec), and SiPho foundries.
>
> > Network Reliability and 'Link Flap': The "Link Flap" phenomenon, where an optical link momentarily blinks, disrupts the synchronization (all-reduce) of the entire AI cluster and leaves GPUs idling. In massive clusters, solutions that guarantee reliability rather than just bandwidth (such as Credo's Zero-Flap) become the ultimate bottleneck determining economic viability.
>
> $TSEM $COHR $LITE $AAOI $MRVL $LITE $TSM $INTC $GFS $FN $SMTC $MTSI $APH $CRDO

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 10 23:40:32 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 296 · ↻ 36 · 💬 13 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2075726900291416365)

> Rosenblatt: Optical
>
> Context Behind Recent Sector Weakness
>
> > China InP Capacity Scare: Stocks traded poorly over the last 1–2 months due to fears that expanding indium phosphide (InP) capacity in China could crash laser pricing.
>
> > CPO Timing Rumors: Reports suggested a potential one-year delay for large-scale Co-Packaged Optics (CPO) deployment compared to the base expectation of a 2H27 build and 2028 shipment.
>
> > Short Seller Dynamics: Checks indicate short sellers are exploiting this mid-quarter noise without genuine conviction. Many plan to cover their positions before 2QCY26 earnings roll out in late July/early August and intend to go long on Optical stocks by 2027 to capture the 2028–2030 CPO ramp.
>
> Assessing the China InP Threat
>
> > Supply vs. Demand: Chinese players could add 20% to 40% to Rosenblatt's 2030 non-China InP laser capacity forecast of ~$26bn. However, total 2030 InP capacity is still projected to fall 40% behind aggregate demand, mitigating oversupply risks.
>
> > Technological Moat: Near-term Western pricing remains secure because Chinese manufacturers currently lack 200G EMLs and high-power CW (continuous wave) lasers required for CPO and Near-Packaged Optics (NPO) applications. They currently possess low-power CWs for SiPo transceivers and 100G EMLs for 800G transceivers.
>
> > Market Decoupling: Long-term Western and Chinese supply chain dynamics are unlikely to be fungible due to political decoupling and the technical shift toward CPO. Western leaders like Lumentum (LITE) and Coherent (COHR) are already fully sold out through 2027 and into 2028, bolstered by major pre-buys from companies like NVIDIA.
>
> Dongshan Precision: Recently greenlit a $1.2bn expansion in Changzhou for InP lasers and 1.6T transceivers after acquiring Source Photonics.
>
> Sanan IC: Pivoting from LEDs to InP, expanding capacity from 2,750 to 6,000 6-inch wafers per month.
>
> HiSense Optoelectronics & Accelink: Also actively growing InP capacity
>
> Architecture & Structural Industry Demands
>
> > CPO Timeline Intact: The smaller-scale CPO timeline (2H26 build, 2027 ship) remains on track, with 2027 production estimates ranging from 30K to over 350K units each for NVIDIA and Broadcom. 2028 remains the definitive volume inflection year for large-scale CPO, with NPO filling the intermediate gap in 2027.
>
> > Network Flattening Already Priced In: Concerns that technologies like Multipath Reliable Connection (MRC) and Resilient Network Graphs (RNG) will hurt demand are overblown. While larger radix Ethernet switches reduce transceivers per switch from 6–7 down to 3–4, exponential XPU volume growth easily offsets the lower ratio.
>
> > Alternative Laser Architectures (GaAs / VCSELs): 200G VCSELs (made from Gallium Arsenide rather than InP) are emerging as intermediate NPO solutions. Broadcom is looking at them for 3.2T NPO platforms, while Lumentum and startup PicoJool have demonstrated VCSEL-based solutions to circumvent potential InP supply constraints in GPU-to-GPU interconnects.
>
> Key Company Earnings Setups
>
> > Lumentum ($LITE): Toughest near-term setup because it has provided the most forward guidance, though it remains highly attractive at ~$700. Investors are watching if it can accelerate its CY27 target of $2bn in quarterly revenue with 40+% operating margins.
>
> > Coherent ($COHR): Highly favored due to accelerating internal 200G EML/CW laser production and a major new ~$1bn/year 1.6T transceiver contract win with Google (sourcing Mitsubishi lasers). Long-term margins will be supported by 11-figure LTAs with NVIDIA for 2027–2030.
>
> > Applied Optoelectronics ($AAOI): Expected to deliver a "beat and raise" watershed 2Q26. Driven by 800G sales to Amazon and Oracle, revenues are expected to exceed $200mn in 2Q26, with 3Q26 guidance pointing to ~$300mn and gross margin expansion well north of the ~30% level seen in 1H26.
>
> > Arista Networks ($ANET): Positioned for strong growth via massive deployment wins with Meta, Microsoft, Oracle, OpenAI/Anthropic, and Google (which could become a 10% customer in 2026). High deferred revenue recognition is expected to fuel >30% revenue growth in 2H26 and 40+% in 2027.
>
> > Fabrinet ($FN): Positioned for solid sequential Datacom growth with NVIDIA alongside initial revenue contributions from new Datacom customers Amazon and Lumentum.
>
> > Viavi Solutions ($VIAV): Safe from InP noise as it has no direct exposure. Growth is driven by testing systems (transceiver/OCS) and MilAero products, with CPO/NPO testing revenues slated to begin this fall.
>
> > Ciena ($CIEN): Ciena's order book suggest that Data Center Interconnect (DCI) and scale-out orders are poised to reaccelerate from previous levels.

> Quantum stocks are seeing a broad pullback today, with all major names in the red.

### Pepe Maltese (@pepe_maltese)
_Mon Jul 13 17:47:57 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/pepe_maltese/status/2076725332581797922)

> Agree, and the "stops too early" part is the whole game. The useful question it's how long it stays one and who collects the rent while it lasts.
>
> That mostly sorts the list. Power and interconnect are a durable one, physically capped by grids, permitting and multi-year lead times, so pricing holds. Packaging and photonics are real but catch-up constraints, capacity is coming, so those rents compress.
>
> Memory is the one I genuinely can't resolve, and you're closer to it than I am. Historically it's the definition of cyclical, supply answers and pricing rolls. The structural case, agentic inference making memory demand persistent instead of bursty, is the most interesting counter I've seen, but I keep getting stuck on whether it actually breaks the pattern or just delays the same capex response.
>
> So I'll flip it to you since it's your wheelhouse: what makes this cycle different, if it is? That's the piece that decides whether memory sits in the durable bucket or the mean reverting one.

>
> "Co-packaged optics is emerging as a critical architectural shift for AI datacenter networking, driven by the rising power, bandwidth, and density constraints of traditional pluggable optical modules."
>

>

>
> > $AVGO and $NVDA in switch platforms. 
>

>

>

>

>

>

>

>
> 🖱 $VPG - Makes force and pressure sensors that help robots interact with the real world.
>
> 🖱 $TSLA - Long-term humanoid robotics play through Optimus, combining AI, hardware, and manufacturing.
>

>
> The robotics market extends far beyond humanoids. The biggest winners could be the companies supplying the hardware and infrastructure every robot depends on.

>
> Quantum computing just took a meaningful step into real-world biology.
>
> "Danish scientists combined a photonic quantum computer with generative AI to design vaccine peptides, then validated the results in the lab."
>
> "Across 131 HLA types, the hybrid system generated stronger peptide candidates than classical AI for 63% of them, with its greatest advantage appearing when training data were scarce."
>
> "This suggests hybrid Quantum + AI could help accelerate vaccine development, personalized immunotherapy and drug discovery for diseases that currently lack sufficient biological data."

### GUL (@gulVasikova)
_Mon Jul 13 18:15:53 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/gulVasikova/status/2076732359916060881)

> AI Infrastructure Spending Continues to Fuel Semiconductor Supply Chain
>
> AI infrastructure stocks moved higher after reports that $META plans to double its in-house computing capacity to 14GW next year, reinforcing expectations that hyperscaler AI capital expenditures remain in a multi-year expansion cycle. At the same time, $MU announced plans to invest more than $250 billion in U.S. semiconductor manufacturing through 2035, further supporting demand across the semiconductor equipment, optical networking, memory, and advanced packaging ecosystem.
>
> For investors, the key takeaway is that AI spending is no longer centered solely on GPUs. Every incremental gigawatt of AI compute requires a massive build-out of servers, networking, optical interconnects, memory, storage, power management, cooling systems, semiconductor manufacturing equipment, and advanced materials.
>
> This broader infrastructure investment benefits companies across the AI supply chain, including $ASML, $COHR, $LITE, $MRVL, $AVGO, $MU, $VRT, $GLW, $POET, $NVDA, $AMD, $ANET, and $SMCI.
>
> Among them, $COHR (Coherent) remains one of the more compelling AI infrastructure beneficiaries. The company supplies critical photonics, optical networking components, lasers, and advanced semiconductor materials that enable high-speed data transmission inside AI data centers. As AI clusters become larger and more bandwidth-intensive, demand for optical connectivity is expected to accelerate.
>
> Fundamentally, $COHR continues to execute well. The company reported 20.5% year-over-year revenue growth in its latest quarter, while Wall Street remains constructive, with TD Cowen, Needham, and Rothschild & Co. maintaining Buy ratings. Current analyst price targets generally range between $395 and $455, implying meaningful upside if AI infrastructure demand remains strong.
>
> Institutional ownership also remains supportive. Recent filings showed $NVDA establishing a significant position in $COHR, while several large asset managers increased their holdings, reflecting continued institutional conviction in AI infrastructure. Although insider selling has continued, the transactions appear consistent with routine profit-taking rather than a deterioration in the company’s business fundamentals.
>
> Investment view: The secular AI infrastructure thesis remains intact. As hyperscalers continue expanding AI data centers, the biggest long-term winners are likely to be companies supplying the critical enabling technologies—not only GPU leaders like $NVDA and $AMD, but also infrastructure providers such as $ASML, $COHR, $LITE, $MRVL, $VRT, $GLW, and $POET that power the broader AI ecosystem.

### charahim94 (@charahim9494)
_Mon Jul 13 18:31:31 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 19 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/charahim9494/status/2076736294328365145)

> Over the years, co-packaged optics (#CPO) has been demonstrated with a variety of 💥light-source architectures, showing that there is no single universal approach. Some notable examples include:
> ✮IBM Power 775 (2010): one of the first commercial CPO implementations, using 850 nm VCSEL arrays
> ✮Hewlett Packard Enterprise’s 2 × 12.8 Tb/s switch demo (2012): also based on VCSELs but different wavelength than IBM (990nm?).
> ✮Rockley Photonics, Broadcom, Cisco, and Ayar Labs: using remote / external CW lasers
> ✮Intel: demonstrating integrated-laser with silicon photonics
> ✮RANOVUS Inc.: using a quantum-dot multi-wavelength laser platform, with both integrated and external-source variants
> ✮Avicena Tech LightBundle: using micro-LEDs, which are also relevant for CPO-style interconnect applications
> Each architecture brings different trade-offs in energy efficiency, reach, latency, cost per bit, and technology readiness.
> The table below summarizes the key attributes of the main light-source choices for CPO. It seems there is no one-size-fits-all answer. The right choice depends on reach, power budget, cost target, packaging approach, and manufacturing maturity.
> P.S: Is my collection of CPO implementations complete? Productive feedback is welcome❤️

> ⚡ ENERGY & STORAGE → powering the buildout: $TE $EOSE $SPKL
> 🚁 AUTONOMY & DRONES → machines that operate themselves: $ONDS $AUR $MRLN $KRKNF
> 🤖 PHYSICAL AI → intelligence that acts: $OUST $AMBA $OSS
> 💡 PHOTONICS → light replaces copper: $CRDO $SIVEF $AAOI $LITE 
> 🏗️ AI INFRASTRUCTURE → the compute buildout: $IREN $NBIS $DGXX $WYFI 
> 🔬 GLASS & OPTICAL MATERIALS → the substrate light runs on: $GLW $LPTH $LPKF
> 📡 CONNECTIVITY & RF → moving the signal: $AMPG
> ⛏️ CRITICAL MINERALS → the hard constraints under everything: $MP $UAMY $ASPI
>
> Here's what the map teaches that a watchlist can't: these aren't nine separate trades. They're one machine → the minerals feed the glass, the glass carries the light, the light feeds the compute, the compute powers the intelligence, the intelligence drives the machines, and the machines reach for orbit. Every layer is a chokepoint for the one above it.
>
> Which is the entire investing philosophy in one image: don't chase the logo at the top of the stack → own the layers everything above is FORCED to buy from. Logos compete. Layers collect.
>
> Important note: a map is a thesis, not a timing tool → layers de-rate together when the factor gets sold (see: this month), and not every name survives to see its layer win. Diversification across a stack is still one machine.
>
> The future economy isn't a sector. It's a supply chain → and it's hiring.

### Nirmātṛ (@En_formare)
_Mon Jul 13 21:17:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 5 · ↻ 0 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/En_formare/status/2076778095147950241)

> Wavelength-scale nonlocal metadevices shatter finite-size Q limits, trapping light like an infinite crystal in a ring the size of a single wavelength while emitting pristine vector beams on demand. Researchers from Harbin Institute of Technology (Shenzhen), Pengcheng Laboratory, and collaborators fused bound states in the continuum (BICs) with topology to engineer nonlocal metasurfaces bent into closed, continuous-boundary rings. 
>
> Traditional finite nonlocal metasurfaces bleed radiation at edges, capping quality factors. Seamless loops eliminate lateral radiative channels, yielding experimental Q factors approaching 10^5 at true wavelength scales and rivaling ideal 1D infinite quasi-BICs. This topological approach conquers the boundary curse. 
>
> Strong meta-atom collective interactions suppress unwanted radiation while preserving controllable vertical emission. Multipole analysis shows the BIC mode dominated by magnetic dipole and electric quadrupole contributions, minimizing leakage unlike the leaky mode’s toroidal and quadrupole-heavy profile. Size-dependent tests confirm saturation at large radii matches the infinite-case limit, with robust fabrication tolerances against grating shifts, overlays, and height variations.
>
> Dual vector beam generation, radial and azimuthal polarizations, plus OAM beams and nonlinear responses from one compact device. On-chip photonics gains high-Q, mode-multiplexing capability for ultra-efficient light trapping in sensors, lasers, quantum tech, and structured-light applications, all in smaller-than-conventional footprints.
>
> Photonic chips can now confine light in whispering-gallery-like modes while emitting engineered vortices on cue, bridging classical confinement with nonlocal coherence. Like bending a leaky fence into an unbreakable Möbius loop, this seamless marriage of metasurface nonlocality and microcavity topology marks a record advance. Points toward scalable integrated photonics that defy size-Q trade-offs.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNIyq5YawAExkbq.jpg

### Cal Conviction (@CalConviction)
_Mon Jul 13 22:01:34 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/CalConviction/status/2076789156349710633)

> $AEHR deep dive:
>
> Financials are ugly backward-looking, but interesting forward-looking. TTM revenue was USD 45.26M, TTM gross margin was 30.72%, free cash flow was negative USD 12.19M, and FY2027 consensus revenue was USD 85.14M, or about 71% growth.
>
> The thesis is that Aehr is becoming a tollbooth for testing the fragile stuff inside AI hardware: high-power AI ASICs, advanced packages, silicon photonics, and optical I/O. If these chips fail inside a data-center system, the customer has a very expensive bad day.
>
> The catalysts are real: Q3 FY2026 bookings were USD 37.2M, effective backlog was USD 50.9M, then Aehr announced a record USD 41M hyperscale AI package-level burn-in order. On June 17, it added a follow-on FOX-XP wafer-level burn-in system order from a major silicon-photonics customer, configured for nine wafers in parallel and scheduled for delivery within six months.
>
> The catch: the new SiPh order value and customer name were not disclosed, and the customer forecast for more systems this year is not backlog until purchase orders show up. At roughly USD 112, the stock was already around USD 3B-plus market cap, with stale analyst targets around USD 64. That is not exactly a bargain bin.
>
> Risks: valuation, customer concentration, bookings-to-revenue timing, gross margin recovery, and the classic small-cap semi equipment problem where everyone falls in love with the order headline before the revenue and margin proof arrives.
>
> Entry/Verdict: HOLD / catalyst watch / no add-size chase. Tiny tracker only if you want event exposure. Real add-size waits for FY2027 guidance above USD 100M-125M minimum, ideally toward USD 140M+, plus backlog conversion, margin recovery, and estimate revisions.
>
> The tech signal is real. The stock just needs the numbers to stop being theoretical. We'll see how it goes.

### CV Research (@CVResearch_)
_Mon Jul 13 22:27:03 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 61 · ↻ 2 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/CVResearch_/status/2076795569649897751)

> $CRDO's board published its own price target in an SEC filing last month. Almost nobody read it.
>
> Buried in a June 8-K: a one-time CEO award. 1.44M shares that only vest as revenue climbs from $2.5B to $7.5B and the stock clears hurdles from $244 to $489 by 2031.
>
> The CEO gets nothing unless shareholders triple first.
>
> Boards don't structure comp like that for companies they expect to grind.
>
> Consider who built this. The CTO spent 11 years leading analog design for $MRVL's storage chips, recovering impossibly faint signals billions of times per second without errors. Same physics as the engine inside every Credo cable. He didn't pivot into a hot market. He transplanted a mastered craft. His stake: $1.3 billion.
>
> The seed check came from Marvell's own co-founder. $3M, now worth about $1 billion. Lip-Bu Tan, now running $INTC, led the round.
>
> Founded, funded, and governed by Marvell royalty. Today, Marvell is chasing them with a copycat cable program. The students became the masters.
>
> The smart money kept coming. To win $AMZN in 2021, Credo granted it a warrant on 4M shares at $10.74. Fully vested, now worth ~$1B. Amazon didn't just pick its cable supplier. It took a billion-dollar equity stake in the outcome.
>
> And the setup nobody connected: the optical supply chain is short of lasers through 2027, bottlenecked by a substrate under Chinese export controls. $CRDO  just spent $1.3B on a photonics architecture that needs far fewer lasers, and its FY28 cable line replaces them entirely with microLEDs made outside the bottleneck. In a two-year famine, the vendor selling the workaround collects scarcity rent.
>

### Serenity (@aleabitoreddit)
_Mon Jul 13 23:17:46 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 909 · ↻ 41 · 💬 118 · [open on X](https://x.com/aleabitoreddit/status/2076808331453415674)

> TLDR of Innolight investor relations takeaways:
>
> 1. "Overall, 1.6T market demand has not contracted; instead, 800G demand has increased significantly compared with previous expectations"
>
> Prob most important takeaway as a whole was 800G demand revision (also longer tail demand). Which is a bullish read through on US transceiver makers like $AAOI, $COHR, $LITE. 
>
> Lot of new customers like neoclouds, AI model companies, contributing to overall demand rather than just hyperscalers, diversification always a bonus. 
>
> 2. Innolight said the shortage covers the module supply chain broadly including:
>
> - Optical chips.
> - Electrical chips.
> - PCBs.
> - Other module materials
>
> From last ER, I think they singled out EMLs and CW optical chips as the most constrained. So Innolight's bottleneck list mention broadened since then. 
>
> They expect some of the component availability to improve gradually from the second half of 2026 through the first half of 2027. 
>
> Think a lot of this is already known from earlier though. 
>
> But just some confirmation + easing timelines (EML is extremely bottlenecked, same with CW, this is probably talking about other components). 
>
> 3.  Innolight said module-production equipment is not the constraint. Equipment lead times remain relatively short. 
>
> So this isn't really a bottleneck compared to others. 
>
> 4. The overall proportion of silicon photonics continues to trend upward. Last year it was mainly 800G. This year, some 800G customers are further increasing their silicon-photonics proportion. 1.6T also added some new customers
>
> Positive for SiPH penetration eg. $SIVE / $JBL, since this shifts away from EML toward CW. 
>
> Basically: main surprising takeaway is just 800g demand go brrr. 
>
> Apart from that just reaffirming bottlenecks/timelines/market speculation.

### Stately (@116sbz)
_Mon Jul 13 23:35:50 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/116sbz/status/2076812877663719505)

> With the explosive growth of artificial intelligence, data centers are demanding increasingly higher computing power. 
>
> Traditional copper cables can no longer meet the extreme high-speed transmission needs of massive data, and they also generate excessive heat. Therefore, "optical communication" (using light instead of electricity to transmit data) has become the key to solving the computing bottleneck.
>
> In this sector, I believe three companies have the deepest "moats" (core competitive advantages) and the greatest future potential. 
>
> Here is a simplified, easy-to-understand breakdown:
>
> Lumentum (LITE): The "Profit Harvester" 
>
> Mastering Core Physics
> Lumentum's core advantage lies in its extremely high "technical barriers" and overwhelming pricing power. Simply put, as tech giants demand increasingly faster optical transmission speeds, it becomes incredibly difficult to manufacture lasers that can work stably at high temperatures while maintaining extremely pure light sources. Lumentum has successfully conquered this physics problem, producing top-tier 200G lasers. Because the technical threshold is so high—competitors either can't make them or can't make them well—Lumentum can sell its products at prices far above the industry average, causing its profit margins to soar. Furthermore, NVIDIA recently invested a massive $2 billion to lock in Lumentum's future production capacity. This means their current situation is one where demand far outstrips supply, and their only worry is manufacturing fast enough.
>
> Coherent (COHR): The "Industry Tollbooth" 
>
> Controlling Core Materials
> If Lumentum wins on the extremely high profit margins of individual products, Coherent's moat is built on "absolute production scale" and "scarce manufacturing capabilities." Currently, the biggest bottleneck in the entire optical communication industry is a shortage of a critical material called Indium Phosphide (InP). Coherent is upgrading its production from traditional smaller wafers to larger 6-inch wafers. This upgrade allows them to produce four times as many devices at once while cutting the cost per device in half. What's most impressive is that they handle everything themselves, from the foundational materials to the final finished products, without relying on others. Also having received a $2 billion investment from NVIDIA, Coherent is transforming from a standard hardware supplier into a foundational "tollbooth" that all AI data center builds cannot bypass. While they are currently spending a lot of money to build out factories, in the long run, this scale advantage will be very difficult for competitors to overcome.
>
> Marvell (MRVL): The "Chip Design Pioneer" 
>
> Leading Next-Gen Architecture
> Marvell's advantage lies in its powerful "ecosystem and chip design capabilities." Unlike the first two companies that build their own factories to manufacture hardware, Marvell focuses on the design of silicon photonics technology and custom networking chips (leaving the actual production to foundries). The future trend is that optical communication equipment will be increasingly and deeply integrated directly with computing chips, and Marvell stands right at the center of this technological architecture shift. They have already successfully shipped over 5 million complex photonic integrated circuits (PICs), proving their strong ability to execute and deliver technology. Marvell has the fiercest upward momentum among these three companies and is the purest play on the combination of custom chips and optical networks. However, it is important to note that precisely because everyone is so optimistic about it, its current stock price (valuation) is already very high, making it a choice where high risk and high reward coexist.
>
> Technical Support of these stock at 200EMA:
>
> $LITE SUPPORT AT 600
> $COHR SUPPORT AT 260
> $MRVL SUPPORT AT 150

### 4FIRE (@netcreat)
_Sat Jul 11 11:57:32 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 12 · ↻ 1 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/netcreat/status/2075912370921328784)

> NSF has already opened two X-Labs funding opportunities, and each eligible lead organization may submit up to two proposals per topic.
>
> The first topic, Quantum Systems: Interconnects and Integrated Photonics, targets the scale-out bottleneck in quantum computing by supporting modular QPU links, heterogeneous quantum-system interconnects, quantum transducers, low-loss photonics, light sources, switches, and single-photon detectors.
>
> The second topic, Scientific Instrumentation for Sensing and Imaging, focuses on next-generation measurement platforms, including quantum sensors, AI-enabled imaging, molecular-scale detection, deep-tissue imaging, and advanced scientific instruments.
>
> Both programs use the same phased X-Labs structure: up to $1.5 million in Phase 0, followed by $10–50 million per year in Phases 1 and 2.
>
> Assuming the maximum annual award and the full 36-month duration in both later phases, the theoretical maximum reaches $301.5 million per X-Lab.
> If a lead organization ultimately secures and fully advances one X-Lab in each of the two topics, the combined theoretical ceiling would be $603 million.
> These figures are not guaranteed allocations, because every phase is subject to Go/No-Go review, milestone achievement, negotiation, and the availability of federal funds.
> The program is therefore much larger than a conventional NSF research grant and is designed to create independent, full-time organizations capable of building commercially relevant platform technologies.
> For comparison, DARPA’s Quantum Benchmarking Initiative offers a theoretical maximum of about $316 million per company across all stages.
>
> In scale, X-Labs is therefore approaching QBI, but its focus is broader: QBI validates utility-scale quantum-computer architectures, while X-Labs funds the enabling platforms that could reshape quantum systems, sensing, and scientific instrumentation.
> https://t.co/SQlLj8HSQi
>
> https://t.co/bYQlLFPwXJ

### ABD Borsa Rehberi (@bugra_kurtoglu)
_Sat Jul 11 12:30:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 21 · ↻ 2 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/bugra_kurtoglu/status/2075920541320384631)

> FOTONİK ŞİRKETLERİ NASIL PARA KAZANIYOR?
>
> Yapay zekâ yatırımları konuşulunca herkes GPU’lara odaklanıyor. Ancak binlerce işlemcinin aynı anda çalışabilmesi için verinin sunucular ve veri merkezleri arasında çok hızlı taşınması gerekiyor.
>
> İşte fotonik şirketleri tam olarak burada devreye giriyor.
>
> Elektrik sinyallerini ışığa dönüştürüyor, veriyi fiber kablolar üzerinden taşıyor ve karşı tarafta yeniden elektrik sinyaline çeviriyorlar.
>
> ✅ Applied Optoelectronics $AAOI
>
> $AAOI daha çok ürünün son kullanıcıya yakın tarafında bulunuyor. Şirket; lazer çipleri, optik alt bileşenler, yüksek hızlı optik transceiver’lar ve kablolu internet altyapısında kullanılan HFC ürünleri üretiyor.
>
> Veri merkezleri için sattığı transceiver’lar, sunucular ve ağ cihazları arasındaki elektrik sinyalini ışığa çevirerek fiber üzerinden taşıyor.
>
> Şirketin gelir modeli oldukça basit: Bir hyperscaler yeni bir transceiver’ı test ediyor, ürünü onaylıyor ve ardından yüksek adetli sipariş vermeye başlıyor.
>
> 400G’den 800G’ye, ardından 1.6T bağlantılara geçiş hızlandıkça satılan ürünlerin kapasitesi ve üretim hacmi artıyor.
>
> $AAOI ayrıca kablolu internet operatörlerine ağ ekipmanı sattığı için yalnızca AI veri merkezlerine bağımlı değil. 2025 yılında gelirlerinin yaklaşık %53,8’i CATV, %42,9’u ise veri merkezi pazarından geldi.
>
> ✅ Lumentum $LITE
>
> $LITE fotonik ekosisteminin daha geniş ve daha çeşitlendirilmiş oyuncularından biri. Şirket yalnızca tamamlanmış optik modüller değil; lazerler, fotonik çipler, optik bileşenler, modüller ve ağ alt sistemleri satıyor.
>
> Müşterileri arasında veri merkezi işletmecileri, telekomünikasyon ekipmanı üreticileri ve ağ altyapısı şirketleri bulunuyor.
>
> $LITE ayrıca yarı iletken üretimi, batarya üretimi, metal kesme, kaynak ve 3D algılama gibi alanlarda kullanılan endüstriyel lazerlerden de gelir elde ediyor. Yani $LITE yalnızca AI veri merkezi yatırımlarına değil, çok daha geniş bir lazer ve optik teknoloji ekosistemine yatırım sunuyor.
>
> ✅ Sivers Semiconductors $SIVE
>
> $SIVE diğer iki şirkete göre daha küçük, daha erken aşamada ve teknolojinin daha özel bir bölümünde yer alıyor. Photonics tarafında AI veri merkezleri için yüksek güçlü DFB lazerler ve lazer dizileri geliştiriyor.
>
> Bu lazerler özellikle co-packaged optics sistemlerinde kullanılabilir. Bu teknolojide optik bağlantılar işlemcilere mümkün olduğunca yaklaştırılarak veri aktarımında enerji tüketiminin azaltılması hedefleniyor.
>
> Şirket ayrıca LiDAR, robotik, üç boyutlu görüntüleme ve biyosensör uygulamalarına yönelik lazerler de geliştiriyor.
>
> $SIVE’nin ikinci faaliyet alanı ise kablosuz iletişim.
>
> Şirket; uydu iletişimi, sabit kablosuz erişim ve savunma sistemleri için mmWave çipleri, anten modülleri ve beamformer ürünleri üretiyor.
>
> Photonics bölümünde gelir ağırlıklı olarak lazer donanımı satışından geliyor. Wireless bölümünde ise şirket hem donanım satıyor hem de müşteriye özel ürün geliştirme sözleşmelerinden gelir elde ediyor.

> AI 瓶頸議題
>
> - 電力瓶頸（Power Bottleneck）
> 類比半導體的時代來臨：
> 摩爾定律不適用的類比領域價值正爆炸性成長，讓供應商擁有壓倒性的定價能力。主要廠商如 TI、NXP、Infineon 已在 2026 年同步執行漲價，證明了這一供應商主導的市場格局。
>
> 12,500 安培與 800V 直流的物理極限：
> 在 600kW 至 1MW 的超高密度 AI 機架中，若繼續使用傳統 48V 供電，電流將暴增至 12,500A，熱損耗將使運作變得不可能。因此，將架構轉移至 800V 以將電流降至 750A，並減少 45% 銅材用量，是物理上的必然選擇。
>
> 垂直供電（Vertical Power Delivery, VPD）：
> 為了避免在「最後一吋」降壓至 GPU 核心電壓（約 0.7V）時產生損耗與電壓波動，VPD——可謂「電源世界的 CPO」——正快速興起，將電源轉換器直接置於 GPU 晶片下方。
>
> - 訊號與光學瓶頸（Signal & Photonics Bottleneck）
> 依距離重新分配銅線與光學：
> 「光學將完全取代銅線」的簡化說法並不正確。實際上是依距離進行重新分配：銅線與類比元件負責短距離（scale-up 領域），光學則接管長距離（機架間連接）。
>
> Semtech 的類比魔法：
> 在 200G/lane 高速通訊中，Semtech 的技術備受關注——它完全省略了耗電高且造成延遲的 DSP，僅使用類比等化器（Analog Equalizer）來修正訊號，將功耗降低十倍，並把延遲從奈秒（ns）大幅縮減至皮秒（ps）。
>
> 光學技術真正的瓶頸在「光源」：
> 雖然 CPO是長期正確方向，但未來 2~3 年現實的贏家仍是 Near-Packaged Optics（NPO）與 1.6T 可插拔模組。光通訊真正的瓶頸位於成品光學模組之下：InP基板、CW雷射光源、由 Soitec 壟斷的 Photonics-SOI 晶圓，以及 SiPho 代工廠。
>
> 網路可靠度與「Link Flap」現象：
> 光學連結瞬間閃斷的「Link Flap」現象，會打斷整個 AI 叢集的同步運算（all-reduce），導致 GPU 大量閒置。在大型叢集中，能保證可靠度而非僅追求頻寬的解決方案（如 Credo 的 Zero-Flap），成為決定經濟可行性的終極瓶頸。

---

### Biology+AI Daily (@BiologyAIDaily)
_Sat Jul 11 13:05:09 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 71 · ↻ 16 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/BiologyAIDaily/status/2075929388613550437)

> Hybrid quantum-classical de novo design of MHC-binding peptides
>
> 1. The study presents an end-to-end hybrid quantum-classical pipeline for de novo design of MHC class I binding peptides, using a real photonic quantum processor to generate latent vectors that seed a conditional GAN.
>
> 2. Core idea: the choice of latent “prior” distribution is treated as a controllable inductive bias. Instead of the default factorized Gaussian noise, the model uses correlated, non-classical priors sampled via Gaussian Boson Sampling (GBS) on a 32-mode photonic device.
>
> 3. Experimental setup: a conditional WGAN-GP is trained on 105,970 mass-spec-validated 9-mer HLA-I ligands (about 77k unique peptides) spanning 126 HLA alleles; the generator is conditioned on HLA labels to learn allele-specific binding constraints.
>
> 4. Priors compared at the same latent dimension (32): classical Gaussian and Bernoulli baselines vs (i) simulated GBS quantum prior and (ii) hardware-measured GBS prior. Quantum-derived priors are rescaled to zero mean/unit variance per dimension to avoid trivial distribution-mismatch effects.
>
> 5. In silico evaluation across 131 alleles (including 5 not in training): the trained generator produces 1000 peptides per allele, and NetMHCpan-4.2 EL %rank is used to call strong binders (threshold 0.5% rank). Across 30 random seeds, quantum priors increase predicted strong-binder yield and reduce variability.
>
> 6. The improvement is not uniform: gains are concentrated in alleles where classical priors perform worst (data-sparse/understudied alleles). A per-allele linear mixed model reports an average improvement vs Gaussian of +10.6 strong binders per 1000 (simulated quantum, p=0.001) and +6.3 per 1000 (real quantum, p=0.049).
>
> 7. Mechanistic signal: for three selected understudied alleles (HLA-A*31:01, HLA-A*68:01, HLA-B*37:01), quantum priors lead to broader exploration at non-anchor positions (higher positional Shannon entropy) while preserving anchor specificity (e.g., basic C-terminus for A*68:01; acidic P2 for B*37:01).
>
> 8. In vitro validation: for each of the three alleles, the top 20 quantum-prior peptides by predicted EL %rank are synthesized and tested using UV-mediated peptide exchange followed by pMHC stability ELISA. Quantum-designed peptides robustly stabilize pMHC complexes; negative-control low-predicted binders fail, and the strongest single binders observed per allele come from the quantum-prior model in the reported comparison set.
>
> 9. Scope and positioning: the authors explicitly do not claim quantum advantage at this scale (32 modes is classically simulable), but argue that hardware-realisable, structured non-classical priors can be a practical inductive bias for peptide generative modeling, especially for rare alleles relevant to personalized vaccines and T-cell therapies.
>
> 💻Code: https://t.co/Dd9SRb1QIL
> 📜Paper: https://t.co/sVD0O7Hm6s
> #ComputationalBiology #Immunoinformatics #MHC #PeptideDesign #GenerativeModels #GAN #QuantumComputing #PhotonicQuantum #HybridAI #VaccineDesign #Neoantigens

### john jacket (@jacket82488)
_Sat Jul 11 14:32:21 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/jacket82488/status/2075951330305474659)

> 【半導体・AIインフラの地殻変動】 「AIの限界はソフトではなく物理（電力と信号）にある」
> 現在、AIクラスターが直面している「電力」と「光・信号」の圧倒的な物理的ボトルネック、そしてその裏で覇権を握る黒幕企業について、Techトレンドをまとめました。
>
> 半導体投資やインフラに関わる人は【ブックマーク】推奨です🧵👇
>
> ⚡ 電力のボトルネック：アナログの逆襲と物理の限界
>
> アナログ半導体の時代到来：ムーアの法則が適用されないアナログ領域の価値が爆発中。TI、NXP、Infineon等の主要ベンダーは2026年に一斉値上げを断行。供給側が圧倒的な価格決定権を持つ市場へシフトしている。
> 12,500Aと800V直流の物理的限界：600kW〜1MW級の超高密度AIラックで従来の48V給電を続けると、電流は12,500Aに激増し熱損失で崩壊する。電流を750Aに抑え、銅材を45%削減できる「800V架構」への移行は物理的な必然。
>
> VPD（垂直電力給電）：GPUコア（約0.7V）への降圧時の損失を防ぐため、電源変換器をGPUチップの「真下」に配置するVPD（電源界のCPO）が急速に台頭。
> 📡 信号・光学のボトルネック：銅の延命と光の現実
>
> 「光が銅を完全駆逐」は誤り：実際は距離に応じた住み分け。短距離（Scale-up領域）は銅線とアナログコンポーネントが粘り、長距離（ラック間接続）を光が担う。
> Semtechのアナログ・マジック：200G/laneの超高速通信において、消費電力と遅延の元凶であるDSPを完全に排除し、アナログイコライザのみで信号を補正するSemtechの技術が激アツ。消費電力を10分の1に、遅延をns（ナノ秒）からps（ピコ秒）へと一気に縮小。
>
> 真のボトルネックは「光源」にあり：長期的な正解はCPOだが、今後2〜3年の現実的な勝者はNPOや1.6T可挿入型モジュール。本当のボトルネックはさらに下流の、InP（インジウムリン）基板、CWレーザー光源、Soitecが独占するPhotonics-SOIウェハ、そしてシリコンフォトニクス（SiPho）ファウンドリにある。
> 網 ネットワーク信頼性と「Link Flap」の恐怖
>
> Link Flap現象がすべてを止める：光リンクが一瞬だけ瞬断する「Link Flap」が発生すると、AIクラスター全体の同期演算（all-reduce）が中断され、膨大なGPUが完全なアイドル状態（サボり）になる。
> 帯域よりも信頼性の時代へ：超巨大クラスターにおいて、単に帯域を広げるだけでなく、この瞬断を絶対に起こさない信頼性を保証できるソリューション（Credoの『Zero-Flap』など）が、AIビジネスの経済性を左右する最終ボトルネックになっている。
>
> 💡 まとめAIの進化は、最先端の1nm/2nmプロセスだけでなく、それを支える「電源（VPD/800V）」や「アナログ信号処理（Semtech等）」、「光源のサプライチェーン（Soitec等）」にいかに強みを持つかで勝負が決まるフェーズに入っています。
> #生成AI #半導体 #NVDA #株クラ #テクノロジー

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM9CujybEAAYGTJ.jpg

> Before a chip ships, it gets "burned in": baked under heat and voltage for hours so the ones destined to fail early die on the test bench, not in the field.
>

>

>

### ᜱ𐤠㇜I ⵉ ᜤ 👽 ᜱ । ⚡︎ । ⚛ ᜤ (@ValienVision)
_Sat Jul 11 16:11:28 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/ValienVision/status/2075976273768137041)

> Physical AI pick-and-shovel ⌁ $NOVT DD  🔖🛸
>
> I spend a loooot of time evaluating the physical AI stack... with perhaps a slightly greater focus on humanoids.
>
> Software models are expanding at an extraordinary pace, yet the immediate scaling constraint remains entirely hardware-bound.
>
> Advanced whole-body control policies require instant, flawless translation into the physical world. 
> It starts with perception, flows through planning and control, then reaches the physical world through motion, force feedback and actuation.
>
> Every stage compounds error, so micro-second precision and adaptive force feedback determine whether an AI brain can function in reality or fail during contact-rich tasks.
>
> The sim2real gap is a hardware execution problem... 
>
> That's why I keep coming back to Novanta.
>
> The company has built an ecosystem that occupies the exact center of this hardware constraint. 
> They deliberately focus on manufacturing the core precision motion, sensing, and also photonics stacks that advanced robotics OEMs require.
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Motion stack
> Precision motion from Celera Motion and Ingenia supplies the encoders (Aura series and IncOder CORE), frameless and slotless high-torque motors (Omni+ line), and certified servo drives (Denali and Everest Safe equipped with FSoE).
>
> The result is (custom) actuators with sub-micron feedback and cogging-free smoothness paired with deterministic real-time control loops needed for stable locomotion and fluid multi-DOF manipulation. 
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Sensing stack
> ATI Industrial Automation (one of their greatest acquisition) contributes multi-axis force/torque sensors from the Axia and Varo families together with automatic tool changers and material removal tools that turn position-controlled arms into systems capable of compliant grasping, adaptive manipulation, and importantly safe human interaction. 
>
> These components matter for collision detection in unstructured environments and for force-modulated actions where pure kinematic control falls short.
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Photonics stack
> The photonics capabilities, built around Cambridge Technology beam steering, Synrad CO2 sources, Laser Quantum solid-state and ultrafast lasers, plus ARGES scanning, support high-precision material processing. 
>
> That matters both for manufacturing the next generation of robots and for the AI-optimized production cells those robots will eventually run inside factories and warehouses.
>
> The laser sources, beam steering, scan heads, and related photonics technologies supplied by Novanta are also used in medical laser procedures, such as ophthalmology, dermatology/plastic surgery, soft tissue applications, and support for minimally invasive/robotic surgery systems.
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Healthcare stack (robotics surgery)
> Continuing on the medical side, WOM insufflators, NDS visualization systems, but also integrated motion solutions underpin minimally invasive and robotic procedures. 
>
> Riverpoint brings high-growth minimally invasive surgical consumables (like advanced surgical fibers, sutures, and implants for trauma and cardiovascular applications).
>
> As AI moves into semi-autonomous subtasks in surgery to autonomous surgery, the same precision motion and force sensing that serve humanoids translate directly into safer, more consistent tissue interaction and better visualization pipelines, and vice-versa. 
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Final thoughts
> What stands out is how the pieces fit together.
>
> Acquisitions stitched a full motion and sensing stack, with end-effector tooling and supporting photonics into one offering. 
>
> That integration reduces risk for OEMs who must hit safety and reliability thresholds for real-world deployments. 
>
> Physical AI patform builders still do the system integration and higher-level control. Novanta supplies the subsystems that let those platforms actually perform at the edge of what physics allows.
>
> $NOVT
